Arts and Entertainment

The Future of Spoken Drama in Shanghai Yang Liu

Some theories in the world seem to remain just theories forever. When those who advocate these theories put them into practice, their work changes direction. It is certainly accurate to say that drama cannot be separated from the masses. Drama is propaganda, it is education, even the most ardent advocates of art for art's sake cannot deny this. The direction that progressive drama practitioners have been striving for in recent years has been in this area. Not only drama, but drama is just a wave in the huge tide of "cultural people going to the masses." But looking at the isolated island, when will this fervent faith go? There are many people engaged in the drama movement, and many drama troupes have been established one after another. However, the object of their work is not the ideal of how to attract a large audience, thus creating a situation where spoken drama has no mass support. Of course, it can also be said that this is due to their weak abilities, but their fatal flaw is not here. In their minds, they despise the audience of the "Living Buddha Jigong" who are full every day, the audience of "Burning the Red Lotus Temple," the masses in the civilized theaters of Tianyunlou and the Great World, and even the audience of the Green Treasure Theater.

The audience of "Living Buddha Jigong" and the civilized theaters have their own historical basis, so let's not discuss them for the time being. The Green Treasure Theater has only been in Shanghai for one or two years, but now it occupies a superior position in the entertainment industry, which is not accidental. In addition to one or two so-called movie stars as a gimmick, the rest of the Green Treasure Theater are still just old characters from civilized theater troupes. However, their performing style is "spoken drama," not "civilized drama." If we want to delve into it, then they have indeed adopted the strengths of civilized drama and put them into the form of spoken drama. Therefore, the success of the same script when performed at the Green Treasure Theater will far surpass that of the current theaters that use spoken drama as a gimmick. Conversely, even without a good script, the Green Treasure Theater can still rely on the actors' "special skills" to maintain itself.

Therefore, professional spoken drama theaters open and close, and it always seems difficult to gain a foothold. Although they have repeatedly failed in business, they can still comfort themselves by thinking: "It is said that the audience in Shanghai is too naive." This idea is certainly justified. Taking the "Swastika Palace" and "Lafayette" in front of us as examples, their hosts are always people with experience in studying drama, but when they stage an unfamiliar script, they have no confidence in success. They cannot establish a strong faith in the audience. After staging an unfamiliar script, the audience shakes their heads and leaves, and to be honest, there are more unsatisfactory scripts than satisfactory ones! After that, the audience they have only has a part of the spoken drama enthusiasts, and the general public will never have a good impression of the clumsy spoken drama.

If spoken drama activists do not focus on winning over the audience, they can only watch it decline day by day. But how can we win over a large audience? In addition to focusing on training actors' skills, the most important thing is a change in psychology -- even if the audience is naive, don't give up on them. The masses are originally naive, but they need to be educated, so that you can cultivate them to have a high level of appreciation. Don't let them only watch "Living Buddha Jigong," and don't let them always be just "the audience of the Green Treasure Theater!"

After Watching Huang Jinrong's New Roles

On the twenty-first day, Huang Jinrong met with people from all walks of life on the stage. The reporter was able to witness the grand occasion and recorded it as follows:

Second Day

To be able to sing, recite, act, and fight, one can be competent. Yanheng can be said to have all four, so the performance is wonderful from beginning to end. "Beating the Drum and Cursing Cao" is Yang Xiaolou's signature play, so of course it is good. Xiaolou's drum has always been called a masterpiece, and no one else can do it. Yuan Shihai's Cao Cao is better than Ma Jun, and there are several Hao school postures when listening to the drum. He is worthy of being a disciple of the Hao family. Mr. Wang from Northeast China Hua Zhi

Since the Huaxin Company filmed the humorous and interesting films "Mr. Wang's Difficulties in Eating" and "Mr. Wang and the Second Landlord," it has aroused a deep impression in the society. Because Mr. Wang and his partners Xiao Chen, Mrs. Wang, Mrs. Chen, and Xiao Ayuan, express the turbulent life of the lower class in the isolated island, it is too incisive. Mr. Wang and other typical characters are from the pen of cartoonist Ye Qianyu. Originally, only people near Shanghai knew him. After he was on the screen, the publicity was wide. Recently, Mr. Wang has appeared in Donglansheng, and people there are said to be filming Mr. Wang's films. The matter started like this. An art magazine called "East Asia Sightseeing," published in Shenyang City, Liaoning Province, reprinted Qianyu's paintings and renamed them "The Unofficial History of Mr. Chen's Trip to Beijing," which tells the story of Mr. Wang and Xiao Chen going to Nanjing to become officials. It is very popular among the general public. Some speculators heard that Mr. Wang's films were very popular in Shanghai, and they also wanted to imitate them, so they planned it. However, they filmed silent films, and there were no standard talents like Tang Jie, so the results were said to be inferior.

Unofficial History of the Pear Garden

Being Clever Turns Out to Be a Joke

As for the fact that Sister Thirteen wrote poems on the wall after that, of course it was not to wipe the blood off the knife out of fear. Besides, she was clearly holding a precious knife that killed people without seeing blood. Except for the possibility that there might still be blood on the handle of the knife, it is a deception to say that blood could be stained on the back or blade of the knife. Furthermore, even if the precious knife was unfortunately stained with blood, it would never be like saving someone from the river, controlling the water for half a day. What's more, it's not enough to control and flick it, and finally wipe it on the sole of the shoe, that's simply cursing Sister Thirteen's precious knife. He would not have thought that He Yufeng was originally a Han Chinese with bound feet, not a Manchurian with big feet. How could the three-inch golden lotus wipe clean the blood stains on both sides of a knife that was four or five inches long and about two feet long? Isn't this another unreasonable absurdity? Looking at this play, it's just a change in the costume of boots and shoes, but it has already caused the above joke. From this, it can be seen that those who advocate reforming old plays must consider everything carefully in order to avoid being ridiculed, but how easy is this!

I once saw Chen Laofuzi (Delin) play the Empress Dowager Xiao in "Visiting Her Mother." Because he often saw the back of the Empress Dowager Cixi when he was serving in the inner court, he also slightly imitated the Empress Dowager's steps and the dignified and generous attitude when he was about to leave the stage in the play, and added the gongs and drums on the stage. It really had a look. Later, Wang Qinnong imitated it and became famous for it. In recent years, even though singers in Beiping such as Zhu Qixiang were far inferior in singing skills, they also won the welcome of the audience by selling these few steps. Who knew that a certain actor who played "Sister Thirteen" would go even further. When he played the role of Empress Dowager Xiao, he staggered every step when he first came on stage, just like the movements and steps of Cao Fu, who played the role of "Tianmen Walks in the Snow." He hunched his back to deliberately show an old and decrepit appearance. (107)
